<div id="review_2013419262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2013419262" />
    <a title="MegaSolipsist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6537806-megasolipsist"><img alt="MegaSolipsist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378520059p2/6537806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013419262?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MegaSolipsist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MegaSolipsist" href="/user/show/6537806-megasolipsist">MegaSolipsist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013419262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12888076451476282028">Wow.<br/>This has to be, hands down, the best piece of superhero fiction ever written. By far. In fact, it may be the best story I have ever read. Certainly, I can't remember a book or series that stuck with me for as long as this one did. It's been eight months now, and my book hangover still hasn't ended.<br/>This is one of the only series that I could legitimately describe as an emotional roller-coaster. My feelings went all over the place while reading it, and any moment spent not reading Worm was one</span>
  <span id="freeText12888076451476282028" style="display:none">Wow.<br />This has to be, hands down, the best piece of superhero fiction ever written. By far. In fact, it may be the best story I have ever read. Certainly, I can't remember a book or series that stuck with me for as long as this one did. It's been eight months now, and my book hangover still hasn't ended.<br />This is one of the only series that I could legitimately describe as an emotional roller-coaster. My feelings went all over the place while reading it, and any moment spent not reading Worm was one bitterly regretted.<br />Worm is the most detailed, consistent and, above all, realistic view of a world with superheroes and supervillains that I've ever seen done. Ever. Possibly the most amazing part about this is that it was written as a blog story, updated twice-weekly, over two and a half years, and comes out as only a fraction smaller than A Song of Ice and Fire and just as complex. It took me two weeks to read it, and would have only taken one if I hadn't had to go to work.<br />Every character was a fully fleshed-out person, people I loved and loathed, with their own flaws and qualities and hopes and fears. There wasn't a single character that I could describe as flat or one-dimensional. Nobody carries an idiot ball and makes bad decisions just for the sake of plot. Every single action carries consequences that reverberate into the future of the series and affect the plot, and these consequences are meticulously thought out and believable.<br />In fact, I would say that 'consequences' is probably a major theme of Worm. It's hard to pin down any concrete themes, as the focus is on a great, believable story, but I would say that beyond the usual links between power and responsibility, Worm shows us that you can do the wrong things for the right reasons, but this doesn't make you a good person. Or that good intentions are meaningless without actions to support them.<br />This series changes a lot as it progresses, starting off as a somewhat dark and realistic look at a world with superheroes and turning into a sometimes cynical deconstruction of the genre as a whole, as well as a hopeful character study, a disaster survival story and even outright horror at several points. I don't think I've ever had a villain truly unnerve me as much as the introduction of Mannequin did, or a monster seem so terrifying as during the Leviathan arc.<br />Possibly the most interesting part of the world of Worm is the trigger events. While a number of people have the potential to develop superpowers, only those who have undergone extremely traumatic events of great physical, psychological or emotional stress trigger and develop powers. The result of this is a skew towards villainy, with even the heroes frequently having deep-seated issues and unresolved problems. And this is precisely what makes Worm stand out from other works in the superhero genre. Because every parahuman in the series, main characters included, is a fundamentally broken person.<br />Whether it's someone being killed with a forced drug overdose, a child slave forced to walk through a mine field or someone being forced to watch their loved ones suffer, nobody emerges unscathed. Paranoia, neuroses, uncontrollable rage, all of them feature in Worm. The main characters are isolated, insecure, sociopathic or suffering from suicidal depression.<br />The main characters also all have fairly low-level powers, and they never pull a victory out of their ass with some contrived deus ex machina or by simply willing themselves to fight harder. You know exactly what most of the superheroes and supervillains can do, and each victory for any of them is hard-earned through cunning and ingenuity. Nobody pulls out a new power as the plot demands, but plenty of them use their established powers in a new way or in a new combination with another parahuman. One of the main things I love about this series is how the most dangerous opponents are never the powerhouses, but rather the force multiplier/synergy combos.<br />None of these things are what makes Worm so amazing (although they certainly help), but rather how they combine and play off each other in incredible new ways.<br /><br />In summary:<br />Incredibly detailed and realistic world.<br />Fascinating and very well-written characters.<br />The different ways that superpowers can be used are far more important than the raw power of them.<br />Intricate and meticulously planned out plot with impressive levels of foreshadowing when you look back at it.<br />The series runs the full gamut of genres, all seen through the lens of a world with superheroes.<br /><br />Now that I've finished Worm, I'm going to have to read the authors next two series, Pact and Twig, because once he finishes Twig he'll be writing a sequel series to Worm, and I need to be ready for that the moment it starts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12888076451476282028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2048585717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2048585717" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34067023-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2048585717?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/34067023-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2048585717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11104204304018922726">It's strange to start a positive review with a list of caveats but I think context goes a long way towards both an appreciation of the accomplishment that Worm is and a healthy idea of whether or not this story is for you.<br/><br/>Worm was a superhero web serial published on a tight schedule. Donation chapters and interludes excepting, there were two chapters every week for roughly two years straight. The amount of herculean effort and commitment that takes is something to be admired.<br/><br/>With that in mind, i</span>
  <span id="freeText11104204304018922726" style="display:none">It's strange to start a positive review with a list of caveats but I think context goes a long way towards both an appreciation of the accomplishment that Worm is and a healthy idea of whether or not this story is for you.<br /><br />Worm was a superhero web serial published on a tight schedule. Donation chapters and interludes excepting, there were two chapters every week for roughly two years straight. The amount of herculean effort and commitment that takes is something to be admired.<br /><br />With that in mind, it's worth noting for people who can't overcome it, this is wonderful storytelling but not articulate literature. Worm is essentially a massive first draft, a monster of a story written by a growing Wildbow. Some chapters are polished and well paced while others suffer from the stressors of the author's day to day life: This is not a story for those who cannot handle the odd typo, flat dialogue or confusing prose. Sometimes what is intended by a paragraph is confusing to grasp and off putting. <br /><br />For everything wrong with Worm's technical polish there is so much done right. This is a story that sells organizational corruption and moral ambiguity as well as it drives home stark, hopeless Lovecraftian horror and frightening conspiracies orchestrating events from the shadows.<br />It is a jaded representation of super hero culture. An articulation of what it means to be a hero or villain in a world where the morality and validity of our actions are unclear.<br /><br />Worm's story is told primarily through the lens of Taylor Hebert. Taylor has recently lost her mother and is severely bullied in school, the trauma of which causes her super powers to manifest. Taylor's powers are simple: She can control every bug within a couple thousand feet of her and she has an enhanced ability to multi-task. These two seemingly weak powers work together in tandem with Taylor's decisive personality and creativity, driving them to their absolute limits. It's the sort of thing I love: A simple idea or ability with countless creative applications, if only the user knows how to manifest them.<br /><br />Taylor just wants to do the right thing but seems to constantly find herself at odds with the wrong people. Early events in the story see her mistaken for a villain and the injustice of that simple fact has immense repercussions for the rest of the story.<br /><br />Unlike the usual super powered universe that may favor simplistic descriptions of powers, most abilities in the Worm universe have some extra layer of complexity or hidden nuance. Most powers manifest through a traumatic event (Something that might seem familiar to Mistborn fans) causing many of those with powers to suffer from psychosis and carry the weight of their traumas with them for the rest of their lives. Some people are warped beyond recognition into near demi-gods that must be constantly monitored and kept away from civilization. Worm is not a story that is afraid to dive into body horror and gruesome descriptions of war.<br /><br />Despite its dark and what some would call edgy tone, Worm isn't a joyless read. It's just so much fun to read about Taylor and her friends learning to utilize their abilities to overcome seemingly impossible odds. There are many of those classic moments when a character is faced with an insurmountable death trap only to connive their way to victory with a clever application of both powers and analytical skills. I personally find these sorts of proactive problem-solving characters inspiring and probably my favorite archetype.<br /><br />Wildbow has a talent for worldbuilding which shines in donation chapters and interludes that explore the world through new point of view characters similar to the interludes between sections of a Stormlight Archive novel. You will quickly find yourself sympathizing with these characters and wishing you got to spend more time with them. Truly it is the mark of a good story if the weight of a side character's story feels real enough that it could have been the main plot.<br /><br />So is Worm for you? If you enjoy a sprawling mammoth of a story that gradually builds from street level heroics to apocalyptic proportions, then yes.<br /><br />Ultimately I have to rate Worm by two standards. As the only web serial I have read, as the first draft of a story, it is remarkably well crafted and sucked me into its world completely, forcing me to give it a 10/10. As a completed work, something I would pick up on the shelf of a store and expect to be polished to superhuman levels? 8/10. There is work to be done here but for those of you who are waiting for the day you see this on a store shelf, I sincerely hope that day comes to pass because this is one hell of a story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11104204304018922726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1622910595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622910595" />
    <a title="Sang Agung" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47717464-sang-agung"><img alt="Sang Agung" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588508106p2/47717464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622910595?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sang Agung" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sang Agung" href="/user/show/47717464-sang-agung">Sang Agung</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622910595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8142947516826373422">Never have a fiction invoked so much emotion in me as Worm had. <br/><br/>Many people would urge you to read this story because it’s a superhero story “done right”; because Worm took the time to ponder on the way superpowers would change our lives should they be real; because Worm constructed its' world in such a believable way where everything is plausible within the context. Yes, Worm is all that; but it is also much more. <br/><br/>In this setting, people with superpowers are called ‘parahumans’. Many would have</span>
  <span id="freeText8142947516826373422" style="display:none">Never have a fiction invoked so much emotion in me as Worm had. <br /><br />Many people would urge you to read this story because it’s a superhero story “done right”; because Worm took the time to ponder on the way superpowers would change our lives should they be real; because Worm constructed its' world in such a believable way where everything is plausible within the context. Yes, Worm is all that; but it is also much more. <br /><br />In this setting, people with superpowers are called ‘parahumans’. Many would have zoomed in on the ‘para’-part and dismissed the ‘human’-part, but in the end, they’re all humans with all the emotions, lives, and baggage humanities bring. Powers does not solve problems. What it does is to accentuate all the part of being a human. Parahumans are not the deific figures they appeared to be in our imaginations. They are, after all, people with powers, and people are flawed at their core. <br /><br />“This world was sublime. A world that was awesome in the truer sense of the word, greater in so many respects. In a metaphorical sense, the peaks were higher, the valleys lower, works of art more artful, extremes more… extreme. It wasn’t a good thing. Make the mountains twice as tall and the chasms twice as deep, and things start crumbling.”<br /><br />Everyone in this story is broken in some ways. The nature of powers makes the moment of trauma to be the central moment in character’s lives. These characters could not ever escape the darkest moment in their life; the irony of their powers makes sure that the trauma would never go away as they used those powers.<br /><br />I recognize that a lot of the characters did bad things and make bad decisions, but it is a testament to the writing that I completely understand what the characters were thinking as they walked those dark paths. Sometimes, I wanted to reach through my computer screen, grab characters by their shoulders, and screamed at them: “STOP IT! Stop doing the things you’ve been doing! It’ll only hurt yourself and the people around you!”. At the same time, I struggled to convince myself that in their shoes—having all the life experience they had with all the traumas—I would be able to do things differently; that I would be able to make all the ‘right’ choices. I have a fantasy where I kidnapped a cadre of psychiatrists, locked them inside rooms filled with all the broken characters, and shouted: “FIX THEM!!”.<br /><br />It’s easy to think that Worm is ‘grimdark’. People often accuse it of taking so much delight in grinding every shred of hope a character might have. Worm says that we are a wretched, petty species, and we have been given the power to destroy ourselves with. In contrast, Worm also told us of the story of heroes. In a world as dark as this, altruistic acts of heroism stood out in stark contrast. I cheered when heroes continued fighting despite the hopelessness around them and cried out as they were being struck down. I jumped out of my seat and hollered when heroes succeeded in pushing back against the tide of despair. The bile in my throat receded as I considered the possibility that the end might not be so nigh after all.<br /><br />I was amazed when I found out that much of the book was an improvisation on the author’s part. In his mind, Wildbow knows that he wanted a handful of scenes in the story. How the character arrived at that scene and how they came out of it, however, was entirely on the character’s hand. Every decision any character made was completely understandable given the context they were in and nothing felt contrived. <br /><br />Wildbow is the type of writer who writes by the seat of his pants. If G.R.R. Martin’s method of getting out from being stuck in a plotline is to stall by fleshing out the world and introducing new plot threads and characters, Wildbow’s method in dealing with being stuck is… to let the characters and circumstances play out on their own. If a central character got presented by a choice and the internally-sensible choice will make the story took on a different, harder course, Wildbow will plunge the story into that course. If a character got on the wrong side of a dice-roll, they die. The story is always on some kind of precipice, ready to plunge you into a wild ride.<br /><br />God, I waxed so much poetry in this review. I love this story so much that I read this behemoth of a story at least seven times from front to back by now. Worm is without any doubt on the absolute top of the list of my favorite story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8142947516826373422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1664547967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664547967" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1893651-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346070700p2/1893651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664547967?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/1893651-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=female-protagonist">female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=superhero-fiction">superhero-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893651-nathan?shelf=written-as-a-serial">written-as-a-serial</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664547967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer545101779216285174">The best superhero story I've ever experienced, of any medium, and one of my favourite of any genre.<br/><br/>I always had a difficult relationship with comic books while I was growing up. I wasn't in the least opposed to getting into them, but the partially-visual nature of the medium obviously cut down on the wordcount, and often resulted in what felt like too short of an experience for me. A voracious reader, I wasn't interested in staring at pretty art for a while; I wanted the story to move along, an</span>
  <span id="freeText545101779216285174" style="display:none">The best superhero story I've ever experienced, of any medium, and one of my favourite of any genre.<br /><br />I always had a difficult relationship with comic books while I was growing up. I wasn't in the least opposed to getting into them, but the partially-visual nature of the medium obviously cut down on the wordcount, and often resulted in what felt like too short of an experience for me. A voracious reader, I wasn't interested in staring at pretty art for a while; I wanted the story to move along, and the small size of your average issue only frustrated me further. It didn't help that, finding it difficult at best to keep up with any given comic series, I often felt like I was missing things (in terms of backstory/character history) when I took a stab at getting into a new comic. Even 'mainstream' stuff like Spider-Man or whatever else was popular.<br /><br />Superhero films are more easily digestible, but cinema has its own limitations too. The length and structure of any given film only allows for so much complexity, and so much time spent with the characters in question.<br /><br />Literature has always been where my heart is, but Superheroes have, for whatever reason, never had much of a presence in that field. I've never yet read a well-written Batman novel published by DC Comics (though looking at the company name, I may have an inkling why) and I think that's a shame. We all know it could be done, it just doesn't seem to happen much, if at all.<br /><br />Worm is perfectly placed as literature; the kind of story that, as people often say, would be ruined entirely by an adaption to film, TV or even graphic novels. It's a long, complex and fast-moving story with an unconventional heroine. The length, complexity and fast pace of the story may in fact be a turn off for some people, as it was for some friends of mine. But for me, Worm transformed the way I think about its genre.<br /><br />Taylor Hebert is a viciously bullied teenaged girl. The bullying, and the sheer cruelty of it, is actually key to the story. Earth Bet, the world the story is set, is essentially an alternate history diverging from ours in the early 1980's, when it's population started receiving superpowers. While it's not entirely common knowledge how people get them, their powers often arise in a moment of extreme trauma, the so called 'worst day of your life'. Accordingly, few people are able to 'trigger' as a new 'Parahuman', and keep a tight enough control on their emotions and morals to go on to become Superheroes.<br />Taylor is one of the few, but the nature of the story includes an examination of what makes you good or bad, so it would be spoilers to go much further into it.<br /><br />Worm's strong points are an incredibly well-developed setting, with a massive and rich cast of characters, and an intriguing story that explores a lot of traditional superhero-genre tropes, subverting many and playing others straight in interesting ways. It bears repeating that this story is loooong, but if you enjoy it like I did I can't imagine you'll be much disappointed by that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="545101779216285174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1102338496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102338496" />
    <a title="♥Xeni♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3584794-xeni"><img alt="♥Xeni♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338844476p2/3584794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102338496?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Xeni♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Xeni♥" href="/user/show/3584794-xeni">♥Xeni♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=free-online">free-online</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3584794-xeni?shelf=2015-books-read">2015-books-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102338496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10367303431276493911">Review from June 15, 2016<br/><br/>----<br/><br/>Review from November 06, 2014 to May 06, 2015<br/><br/>How do you review a novel that is essentially 10 books in one long series? I have no idea, but I'll give it a shot.<br/><br/>First off, this is an amazing book. And it's free on the internet (it's a webseries) so definitely check it out if you're at all interested in superheroes, villains, powers, robots, murder, mayhem, gigantic beasts wreaking havoc and a doomsday prophecy!<br/><br/>That all said, none of that actually does the tale justice</span>
  <span id="freeText10367303431276493911" style="display:none">Review from June 15, 2016<br /><br />----<br /><br />Review from November 06, 2014 to May 06, 2015<br /><br />How do you review a novel that is essentially 10 books in one long series? I have no idea, but I'll give it a shot.<br /><br />First off, this is an amazing book. And it's free on the internet (it's a webseries) so definitely check it out if you're at all interested in superheroes, villains, powers, robots, murder, mayhem, gigantic beasts wreaking havoc and a doomsday prophecy!<br /><br />That all said, none of that actually does the tale justice. Wildbow made something incredible when he wrote Worm, and it is seriously good. Not only is the writing superb (aside from some areas that could use a bit of editing, but hey, it's a webseries and not published yet), but the plot takes amazing twists and turns you really don't expect. <br /><br />It's a bit like when you read Game of Thrones and Ned Stark dies in the first few chapters and you're left wondering 'what's next?'. Or when Sanderson dumps the everything you suspected might happen into the first 100 pages of his Words of Radiance and you wonder what could possibly still occur. And then everything that happens is better than you could have ever hoped for. <br /><br />That feeling is also here in Worm. And it's so good. Because yeah, it's a death and doomsday tale and lots of grimdark happenings occur, but the plot really makes it feel worth it. <br /><br />Plot aside, the characters were excellent as well. I started out thinking it was just another teen / highschool coming of age story, but that's just the first few sections. After that it's definitely twisted into something more. Taylor Hebert is our main character, and her power is that she can control bugs. This sounded completely lame to me, but once you see all the crazy shit she gets up to, well, it slowly becomes one of the coolest powers out there. I wish there had been some pov's from more characters; more deeper insights into their minds / powers. There's a lot of that going on, but still. With hundreds of people showing a myriad of powers, it would be nifty to see how they deal with them. Don't get me wrong, we got a lot of that, but the story also focused a lot on Taylor, who irked me with her ways. <br /><br />My favorite capes would have to be Miss Militia (I loved her background story), Contessa (when her actual role was revealed, I was seriously stoked), Tattletale (the way she pisses everyone off is awesome), Clockblocker, etc etc. I can't even remember them all right now. <br /><br />What else is there to say? The tale is amazing. It took me 6 months to read (because breaks in between to get over some of the shit that goes down and it's just hella long) and I wish the journey wasn't over. Worlds are destroyed. People are dead. But what happens next? Who knows. Probably the same old, same old humanity fighting itself to pieces. I'll let my imagination take a more peaceful course for the beloved characters, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10367303431276493911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1563276227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563276227" />
    <a title="Susmita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29493399-susmita"><img alt="Susmita" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563276227?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susmita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susmita" href="/user/show/29493399-susmita">Susmita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29493399-susmita?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563276227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10713829835353645126">TLDR: This book is going to satisfy your superhero fantasy craving like no Marvel Comics movie has ever done before. Do yourself a favour and read it if you want to know what superhero fantasy really feels like.<br/><br/>Worm was the first superhero fantasy novel that I read. Before Worm I have had brief but entertaining encounters with popular superhero movies. So when I began reading Worm, I was not expecting anything particularly out-of-this-world. Simply because I did not know what I could expect from</span>
  <span id="freeText10713829835353645126" style="display:none">TLDR: This book is going to satisfy your superhero fantasy craving like no Marvel Comics movie has ever done before. Do yourself a favour and read it if you want to know what superhero fantasy really feels like.<br /><br />Worm was the first superhero fantasy novel that I read. Before Worm I have had brief but entertaining encounters with popular superhero movies. So when I began reading Worm, I was not expecting anything particularly out-of-this-world. Simply because I did not know what I could expect from it. And at 6,000 pages, Worm was not my first choice of book to read. I still picked it up because R read and was so taken by the book that he wanted me to experience the pleasure of reading an <i>epic action-packed superhero drama</i>. <br /><br />So I began in February and I spent seven months getting to know Taylor Hebert and becoming invested in her story. From the get go Worm was unputdownable. Wildbow created a world and characters that are so endearing that as a reader I wanted to justify the fatal flaws of key characters. <br /><br />The action sequences sometimes confused me and I did not know what I was reading or where the characters were and what was happening. And I guess action sequences are like that. Wildbow tries to put the reader at a vantage point to get a complete view of the battle ground where multiple teams of superheroes are fighting or strategising. So it is only fair that I was a little confused at some points. When the world is coming to an end, fights are bound to become complex and will involve a number of steps to actually give the final blow to the supervillain. So, full marks to Wildbow for showing me what superhero fights are really like. <br /><br /><b>I cannot watch another superhero movie and not wonder what Taylor Hebert would have done.</b> <br /><br />Worm is a superhero fantasy alright, but at the core Worm is the story of Taylor Hebert, a school girl who is a victim of bullying. For me Worm would not have been half as impactful if not for Taylor's backstory and her struggle with wanting to be a better person than those who bullied her. <br /><br />There is so much about this book that is amazing. With every Arc Wilbow increased the stakes and turned characters from white to gray to black. A superhero is willing to do what others will not do to save humanity. Wildbow beautifully explores this quandary of the superhero. <br /><br /><blockquote>I was left with a decision to make, no time to make it. Was I going to be moral, or efficient?</blockquote> <br />There is so much to say about this book, but I am a bundle of random thoughts rights now. I will stop here before I start weeping because I just finished the best superhero fantasy book ever. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10713829835353645126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1563276227">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_758073254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/758073254" />
    <a title="Gints" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8135366-gints"><img alt="Gints" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331490914p2/8135366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/758073254?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gints" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gints" href="/user/show/8135366-gints">Gints</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of rational ideas, superheroes, fantasy in general.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer758073254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11048144670586588024">Oh my! Worm is not your basic empowerment fantasy superhero story. It's also not an ignorant grimdark world of pain. It is thoughtful and aware. It is fell and wonderous. It worms its way from crisis to crisis to crisis of a different kind. From a world-ending threat to a character-ending threat, which is more scary. You keep hoping that things will get better, but they don't. And even when you're sure that this is how the story goes, you keep hoping that Taylor ends up alright. Yet it keeps alw</span>
  <span id="freeText11048144670586588024" style="display:none">Oh my! Worm is not your basic empowerment fantasy superhero story. It's also not an ignorant grimdark world of pain. It is thoughtful and aware. It is fell and wonderous. It worms its way from crisis to crisis to crisis of a different kind. From a world-ending threat to a character-ending threat, which is more scary. You keep hoping that things will get better, but they don't. And even when you're sure that this is how the story goes, you keep hoping that Taylor ends up alright. Yet it keeps always escalating and always teasing with a ray of hope.<br />Wildbow is a master of tension, giving respite when it's needed, only to crank things up soon after. More than that, he's a wirter with a productive combination of imagination and analysis, a surprisingly rare trait among superhero authors. At least when it comes to the applications of various powers.<br /><br /><br />–––Potential spoilers–––<br /><br />I really enjoyed the overall flow of Taylor's narrative. The way you're always wishing for her to succeed, for people to finally listen and cooperate. Yet almost every victory she achieves is followed by a terrible loss. While there is a bit of plot armor as she is the viewpoint character (most of the time), she does get hurt in grievous and permanent ways. Sometimes it's as simple her enemies ending up better off than before their confrontation. Other times it's a further escalation, taking her away from goals, things and people she cares about just to maintain a chance that she'll maybe someday have the opportunity to get back to them. <br /><br />Extra respect to wildbow for handling the ending so masterfully. You expect Taylor to finally catch a break. But she doesn't. But she does. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11048144670586588024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer4598216435189507210">I can move on with my life now. Probably.<br/><br/>Worm was pretty amazing. Fast-paced, engaging, mind-blowing at times, provocative even. And it had perspective. A lot of it, at such a scale... I like perspective.<br/><br/>So much sleep was sacrificed because of Worm. At nearly 7000 pages, I was a slave of the story for quite a while.<br/><br/>It was all worth it. Go ahead and lose yourself in it if you dare.<br/><br/>Just be ready.</span>

<div id="review_2114727132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2114727132" />
    <a title="Snoopy Dogg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65707747-snoopy-dogg"><img alt="Snoopy Dogg" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2114727132?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snoopy Dogg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snoopy Dogg" href="/user/show/65707747-snoopy-dogg">Snoopy Dogg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2114727132&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2114727132" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1132138634296080677">Note: there will be spoilers ahead. Most will be minor, but certain twists led to me lowering my score, and will be discussed.<br/><br/>I wanted to like it, I did. The setting is pretty much made for me, and I really liked the idea of the Endbringers, unstoppable forces of nature that really set the tone of the series I feel. Certain characters stole the show whenever they appeared, and <br/><br/>Starting off I was 100% on board with Reddit's "This is the best book ever written" hype. Certain chapters genuinely str</span>
  <span id="freeText1132138634296080677" style="display:none">Note: there will be spoilers ahead. Most will be minor, but certain twists led to me lowering my score, and will be discussed.<br /><br />I wanted to like it, I did. The setting is pretty much made for me, and I really liked the idea of the Endbringers, unstoppable forces of nature that really set the tone of the series I feel. Certain characters stole the show whenever they appeared, and <br /><br />Starting off I was 100% on board with Reddit's "This is the best book ever written" hype. Certain chapters genuinely struck chords with me, most notably Hive when Taylor confronts the teachers about the bullies. The fights were good, the powers creative, and the story interesting. This culminates in the Leviathan arc, my favorite arc of the story. All seemed well.<br /><br />But, and this is a rather large but, over time whatever goodwill I had for the protagonists vanished, until by the Echidna arc I was rooting against them. In fact even before that I was hoping Coil would succeed in some way, and when you're supporting a kidnapping, torturing, gives-drugs-to-little-kids-to-basically-enslave-them sociopath over his opponents you know something's not right.<br /><br />So what happened? I find it hard to pinpoint exactly, but I've noted some factors which, while they may not be exhaustive, help to explain why Worm lost its allure.<br /><br />First, there's the characters, most notably Tattletale and Taylor herself. I loathed Tattletale. Her interactions with Panacea in the bank and then again later on in the Slaughterhouse Nine arc display how callous she really is, and the story glosses over this. When discussing Victoria's fate, the impact of the Undersiders on her mental state, which directly led to the above, is almost never mentioned. Tattletale is the corruptor to Taylor, which is fine, but the story never addresses it. TO make matters worse, for a considerable amout of time the audience only has her word for it that certain events happened the way they did. Surely someone who's MO is manipulation would never lie?!<br /><br />Tattletale's near-omniscience was also a massive deal-breaker for me. The only time her powers mislead people and any consequences actually arise from it is in the bank. Which is her first time working with Taylor. That's it. She then proceeds to whip up oh-so-convenient solutions to the Slaughterhouse Nine, Coil, and Echidna arcs. Those arcs are consecutive, by the way, so finding out that she has magically resolved yet another crisis was utterly maddening.<br /><br />Then there's Taylor herself. While not as bad as Tattletale, her constant self-aggrandising gets real old real fast. Taking the moral high ground when the S9 are rampaging around is one thing. Doing the same against Cauldron is outright hypocritical, but nothing surprising. Blackmailing the heroes because of the "greater good"? Yeah, that's too far. <br /><br />Her underdog status, and that of the Undersiders as a whole, also stops being an actual thing quite quickly. When you're defeating members of the S9 one-on-one, twice, and when the entire group survives multiple crises unscathed while other teams (who are conveniently opposed to the Undersiders) are ravaged by them, you are not the underdogs. When you are the de facto rulers of a city, you are not the underdogs. Would be nice if the story stopped pretending they were.<br /><br />Most of my remaining quibbles are to do with the plot, and I'll try to be quick about it, so here goes.<br /><br />The reveal of the Endbringer's origins and motives was extremely aggravating. I always think the twist of "X was holding back the whole time" is a sign that the author has written himself into a corner by making character X too powerful. (Especially when the book was sold to you by saying that this wouldn't happen.)<br /><br />The bullies are cartoonishly over the top, to the point where they're too much so to make Taylor sympathetic by comparison.<br /><br />The deus ex machina that saves the team in the S9 arc was infuriating and touches one of my pet hates in fiction. <br /><br />The treatment of Shadow Stalker is irritating both for Taylor's moralizing and Tattletale's nonsensical abilities.<br /><br />Ultimately I can't really recommend this. It's just kinda meh. And when that meh is spread over 1.6 million words, it becomes grating and you wish you were reading something else. So I did.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1132138634296080677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1121634908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121634908" />
    <a title="Victor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5971628-victor"><img alt="Victor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356813891p2/5971628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121634908?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victor" href="/user/show/5971628-victor">Victor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121634908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9586423148875993798">Well, this sure was something. It's hard I think to really talk about this thing. It starts off very impressive and then veers off course somewhere in the second quarter. By the halfway mark, though, it finds its stride again and is an intense ride all the way through the end.<br/><br/>Honestly my major gripe with this is wilbow's prose. It's... Clunky, for the entire duration. Some odd phrasing choices. Can't say I fault the guy, but it makes for awkward reading at times. And when something is as long as</span>
  <span id="freeText9586423148875993798" style="display:none">Well, this sure was something. It's hard I think to really talk about this thing. It starts off very impressive and then veers off course somewhere in the second quarter. By the halfway mark, though, it finds its stride again and is an intense ride all the way through the end.<br /><br />Honestly my major gripe with this is wilbow's prose. It's... Clunky, for the entire duration. Some odd phrasing choices. Can't say I fault the guy, but it makes for awkward reading at times. And when something is as long as Worm is, the awkward stuff really grates.<br /><br />Wildbow's inventiveness with the super powers and the heroes and villains who use them was easily what kept me reading. The constant escalation of threats the characters face makes chapters fly by at times. That being said, I feel like 75% of the book or maybe more is description of a fight. So if you like fights, you should read this cause you will be in heaven. For me, fights started to get a bit exhausting. Wildbow is great at keeping them fresh though.<br /><br />Taylor is the perfect point of view character, even though she may be the least likable person in the book. Wildbow represents her and her decision making very well. When Taylor starts hatching a plan during a seemingly unbeatable situation, I can't help but get pumped.<br /><br />All in all, I would have to recommend this. There are enough great characters to make it worth getting used to Wildbow's prose and undying affection for giant super hero battles. Yeah it's long, but it's good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9586423148875993798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506532834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9697661571584268114">I honestly don't know how to begin.... What an experience this was... I seriously don't have words to describe how awesome this book is. And god this review is so hard to write without giving away something. <br/><br/>This <a href='https://parahumans.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Web-serial</a> is HUGE. The ebook version I found had was 5708 pages. Needless to say I was terribly intimidated by the size of the book and I thought it would take me forever to finish. However, the book is split into 30 arcs (plus an epilogue arc) and the first arc was just about 50 pages</span>
  <span id="freeText9697661571584268114" style="display:none">I honestly don't know how to begin.... What an experience this was... I seriously don't have words to describe how awesome this book is. And god this review is so hard to write without giving away something. <br /><br />This <a href="https://parahumans.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Web-serial</a> is HUGE. The ebook version I found had was 5708 pages. Needless to say I was terribly intimidated by the size of the book and I thought it would take me forever to finish. However, the book is split into 30 arcs (plus an epilogue arc) and the first arc was just about 50 pages so I thought I'll try it out, and read more only if I like it. I couldn't put it down until I reached Arc 3. I had to forcibly stop reading somewhere in the middle to get some work done. <br /><br />Maybe a mild spoiler alert now but what's here should not hurt the reading experience at all. <br /><br />The book is set in a world where people with super-powers are in plenty. A lot of these parahumans are part of the protectorate, and a lot others are villians. So obviously there are people who can fly, people with super-strength, people who can create fire etc. Sounds like a typical story right? <br /><br />Then, there are some of these super-powers that are pretty unusual. For example, the protagonist, a young teenager called Taylor Hebert, has the power to control insects. You might wondering what good would that be in a world where there are people with obviously stronger abilities. That's what I felt too, and boy was I mistaken.<br /><br />The story almost entirely is from the perspective of Taylor and her <i>growth</i>. She has to face challenges with completely ridiculous odds against her and it only gets more insurmountable as the story progresses. <br /><br />There are tonnes of plotlines, wonderfully woven together with a gazillion characters with all sorts of abilities. Oh and the author just refuses to end a chapter on a calm note! Every damned chapter ends in a cliffhanger!<br /><br />Highly, highly, highly recommend this to everyone who... well I'll recommend it to everyone! Read the first Arc and see if you like it. If you do, I guarantee that you would not be disappointed. <br /><br /><br />An advice to the readers: It is only natural that you might occasional lose track of who is who. Just stay with the flow and quite likely you would soon be able to place things properly. <b>Do not, under any circumstances, search online for <i>anything</i>! You definitely do not want spoiler to ruin the wonderful experience that awaits.</b> Believe me. <br /><br />I know for sure that I'm going to read this again in the near future. What an experience this was. Wow! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9697661571584268114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2KKc+7HovzXdsRMh0Lt5EcTvBSlwYC/I7m2m6ZtJ5e3ihPUpCrZ2XXqap0AnTnPOErDi4b7toa+1E+BYVgoXdw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
